British Public Bus Workers Go on Strike Again Yesterday 161

Opposing the Company's Dismissal of a Large Number of Workers

All Routes Except 1 and 9 Were Completely Suspended Yesterday

The 110 ticket sellers of the British Public Bus Company who had resumed work went on strike again yesterday. Public buses within the concession, except for routes 1 and 9, were completely suspended. The strike committee was reorganized, and a workers' congress will be held today. The various situations yesterday are recorded below:

▲ Strike Again After the 110 ticket sellers of the British Public Bus Company unconditionally resumed work on the 29th, the remaining 152 ticket sellers were completely dismissed by the company. The strike committee sent representatives to negotiate with the company, but the company refused. The ticket sellers who had resumed work went on strike again yesterday due to (1) the company reducing all ticket sellers' wages to 20 yuan, (2) the company canceling the previous bonus system, (3) forcing ticket sellers to provide fingerprints, and (4) supporting the dismissed workers.

▲ Suspension of All Routes After the ticket sellers went on strike again, public buses in the Public Concession, Route 2 (Er Yangjing to Park Shooting Range), Route 5 (Sanmaoge Bridge to North Railway Station), and Route 10 (Caojiadu to Yinxiangxiang) were completely suspended. In order to maintain traffic, the company reluctantly operated buses with newly recruited ticket sellers and shortened the routes. Routes 1 (Jing'an Temple to Laobaizi Road) and 9 (Jing'an Temple to Tilam Bridge) had fewer vehicles than usual.

▲ Unemployed Congress More than 150 ticket sellers dismissed by the company held a general meeting near the company on Kangnuot Road the day before yesterday. More than 120 workers attended. The chairman first reported the process and resolved to (1) organize an unemployed workers' struggle committee, (2) appoint ten committee members, and (3) continue to fight the capitalists to achieve final victory.

▲ Congress Today After the ticket sellers who had resumed work went on strike again yesterday, in order to discuss how to deal with the company, it was decided to convene a workers' congress at 9:00 AM today. It is reported that the drivers also sent representatives to attend. The strike committee was also reorganized, with the number of committee members being 17, including five working ticket sellers, six unemployed ticket sellers, and six drivers. They began working immediately.

Telegraphing for the Cancellation of Feng Shaoshan's Arrest Warrant Approved 165

The National Government Has Already Telegraphed Yu Qiaqing and Others

Huadong News Agency reports that Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jili, Wen Lanting, and others previously believed that Feng Shaoshan, former president of the General Chamber of Commerce, was suspected of being affiliated with warlords and was wanted by the National Government authorities. Now that the National Government's amnesty decree has been promulgated, the cancellation of Feng's arrest warrant has not yet been formally announced. Therefore, last month, they jointly telegraphed the National Government to approve the cancellation of the arrest warrant and restore his freedom. The National Government telegraphed the Shanghai Special City Party Department to investigate and reply. The City Party Department has complied with the order and replied. The State Council has resolved that since there is no definite evidence that Feng Shaoshan is against the government and he meets the amnesty decree previously issued by the National Government, his request to restore his freedom should be approved. However, instead of issuing a formal decree, the National Government telegraphed Yu Qiaqing and four others. Mr. Yu received the National Government's telegram yesterday and immediately telegraphed Feng's family in Beiping.

Ministry of Industry Explains the Issue of Branch Office Staff of the Chamber of Commerce 166

The City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the branch offices in Wusong, Jiangwan, and Pudong yesterday, stating: "Regarding the case, the Industrial Gazette published by the Ministry of Industry, issue 32, in the command column, contains a directive explaining the doubts of Article 8 and Article 19 of the Chamber of Commerce Law submitted by the Yunnan Construction Department. The original text of the directive states, 'Noted. Regarding Article 8, Paragraph 2 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, the so-called 'member meeting' refers to the 'member congress' in Article 24. The so-called 'staff' in Article 3 of the same law refers to the staff selected according to law. The old Chamber of Commerce Law is no longer applicable, and there is no question of publicly electing a chairman. If the executive and supervisory committee members of the Chamber of Commerce reside or operate within the area of the branch office, the Chamber of Commerce may separately elect staff, or, according to the provisions of Article 23 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, appoint clerks to handle the affairs of the office. In case of major events, the matter must still be referred to the staff of the Chamber of Commerce for execution. The number of personnel should be determined by the members' congress according to the complexity of the affairs and Article 29 of the Implementing Rules of the Chamber of Commerce Law.' It is hereby noted that this directive is related to the office standards and organization of the office. Please take note."

Ningbo Compatriots Assist in Building the Ningbo Laojiang Bridge 170

Lv Hu Ningbo compatriots Le Zhenbao and Zhang Jiguang recently went to Ningbo to inspect the Lao Jiang Bridge and plan the reconstruction project. After arriving in Ningbo, County Magistrate Chen of Yin County and Engineer Hu met with them to discuss the construction of the Lao Jiang Bridge. According to Mr. Le and Mr. Zhang, the current of the Lao Jiang Bridge is so turbulent that if it is entirely constructed with cement and steel, there will be many piles, and the current will be even more turbulent, and navigation will be even more inconvenient. It is now proposed to change the bridge body to a steel structure, and the piles and piers will still be made of steel and cement, so that the number can be reduced, and the current may be able to remain the same. Also, the Jiangdong Yangmu wedge must be rebuilt, otherwise, in the event of a large tide, the current of the Lao Jiang Bridge will be even more turbulent. After consultation with County Magistrate Chen and others, it was decided to use three wedge doors made of steel and cement, each with a width of 13 square feet. The old stone materials in the wedge will be used to open a small wedge in front of Sangjia Liangting to store water for irrigation. As for the funding, it will be donated by gentlemen according to the amount of their fields, and the administrative organs will be asked to monitor it strictly.

Urging Wenhua Villa to Switch to Using Chinese Concession Tap Water 172

Wenhua Villa on Shigaota Road was contracted by the owner, Zhidong Company, to Chen Xinji Construction Factory, and construction began in June of the 19th year. After the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau received the notice from the Public Works Bureau that the water and electricity of the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company had not yet arrived, it sent a letter to the owner instructing them to sign a bond before temporarily using water and electricity from foreign water and electricity companies. The owner then submitted a bond for filing. In late August, the Public Utilities Bureau received a request from the Shanghai Waterworks Company to dig roads and requested to dig roads and connect pipes there. For the sake of caution, the construction factory was instructed to sign a bond, stating that "this water is temporarily connected for the construction of houses, and will be removed upon completion of the project." The road digging permit was then forwarded to the Public Works Bureau for approval and construction to connect the water. According to recent reports, the house has been completed for five months, and Zhabei tap water has also arrived, but the water used for construction has not been cut off and is being used to supply residents with drinking water. The water fee is calculated at 7.5% of the rent and collected by the owner when collecting the rent each month, which is a violation of the previous agreement and hinders sovereignty. It is reported that the owner has been ordered to switch to Zhabei tap water before September 10th, and the construction factory has been ordered to remove the installed water pipes within the same deadline, otherwise, they will be severely punished.

Xinjiang Linxi Suspends Mailing 173

The local postal authorities say that banditry is rampant between Xingxingxia and Hami. Heavy-class mail and parcels to Xinjiang are currently suspended. Light-class mail will be temporarily sent via Siberia, otherwise, it will be delayed for a long time en route. They also say that the Eurasian airmail plane cannot currently land in Linxi, so airmail to that location is also temporarily suspended.

Shanghai Pictorial Great Innovation 174

Lowering Prices and Enriching Content

Since the Shanghai Newspaper on Wangping Street was published in 1925, seven years have passed in an instant. It is the only surviving pictorial among the three-monthly publications in Shanghai. Now, to improve printing, retail sales will use high-quality rolled newspaper, costing only four copper coins per sheet. Subscribers will use 100-pound coated paper, which is exceptionally beautiful. The subscription fee remains the same and does not increase. The content also strives to be enriched. In addition to carrying Mr. Zhang Henshui's novels, many well-known people in the news industry have been hired to write, so that readers will be impressed.

Local News II

The Largest Liner in the Pacific Arrives in Shanghai 185

To Invite All Sectors to Visit on the 18th

The Fastest and Largest Postal Ship Between China and America

Since last year, British, Japanese, and American shipping companies have been investing heavily and competing to build giant ships to vie for Pacific shipping. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and Nippon Yusen Kaisha's newly built large postal ships for the China-America route have already been completed and put into service. The American Dollar Steamship Lines has also specially built two new, powerful, and fast postal ships at a cost of 60 million yuan to add to the Pacific route. The first ship, the President Hoover, has already left the factory and set sail. After this ship sails, it will be the largest ship ever on the China-America line. Its speed, hull, and layout are superior to those of the new British and Japanese ships in every way. It is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the 18th of this month, at which time all sectors will be invited to visit. Details are as follows:

▲ Enormous Ship Body The President Hoover and the President Coolidge, built by Dollar, each have a displacement of 31,000 tons and a cargo capacity of 23,000 tons. The ships are 635 feet long and 81 feet deep, with a total of six decks. They are fully equipped with lounges, dining rooms, swimming pools, gyms, smoking rooms, libraries, and more. The first-class section has 350 rooms, the special-class section has 150 rooms, and the third-class section has 700 rooms. The interior layout is exceptionally beautiful, truly like an Atlantic postal ship. Due to the large number of passengers it can accommodate, the ship is equipped with three chief officers. The ship's speed is 23 knots per hour, with a normal speed of 21 knots per hour. A circumnavigation of the world would only take 85 days.

▲ Visit to Shanghai The President Hoover was completed first and set sail from New York on August 6th. The Shanghai office received a telegram stating that all classes of cabins are fully booked on this maiden voyage to Shanghai. It is currently in the Pacific and will arrive in Japan shortly. It is scheduled to enter the port at 9:00 AM on the 18th of this month and dock at the China Merchants Bureau's North Wharf. Dollar has specially appointed his second son, Mr. Harold Dollar, to sail on the ship as a supervisor to China. On the day of arrival in Shanghai, from 3:00 PM to 5:30 PM, all sectors of Shanghai will be invited to visit the ship. 4,000 invitations have already been sent out. The Dollar's general manager, Mr. Stein, and the Chinese director will be on the ship to receive guests and guide the tour. During the tour, all work will be suspended for three hours.

▲ Delayed Aircraft Installation According to Mr. Dollar's plan, two aircraft were originally planned to be installed on the ship, following the Atlantic model, to pick up and deliver express mail and to transport passengers who were unable to board the ship on time by plane to catch up on the high seas, allowing passengers to save even more time. However, due to various reasons, the installation of this type of seaplane has been temporarily delayed. The ship's cargo holds each have special facilities, such as silk cabins, tea cabins, refrigerated rooms, and bullion vaults, which are very well-equipped. The engine is electric-powered, so the fuel is oil.

▲ Maiden Voyage Schedule The ship is scheduled to depart for Hong Kong and Luzon on the 19th, and return to Shanghai on October 2nd. The maiden voyage to the United States will depart from Shanghai. It will take 36 days to reach the United States. The first, second, and third class cabins on the ship are currently fully booked. It is expected that the ship will be full of passengers when it departs from Shanghai. As for the first export cargo loaded on the ship to the United States, even though the market is not good, it can still carry 1,500 tons to the United States. The second new ship, the President Coolidge, which is the same size as the President Hoover, is scheduled to depart from the United States in November and arrive in Shanghai in mid-December. It is said that Mr. Dollar will send his eldest son, Mr. Stanley Dollar, to supervise the voyage when the ship begins its service.

A Fine Young Man Attempts Suicide for a Woman 186

A Passionate Romance Between a Man and a Woman

Marriage Opposed by Parents

Li Junfu Takes His Own Life Because of This

The Police Station Offers Guidance

Li Junfu, a local resident, 19 years old, recently became disheartened due to an unsuccessful marriage proposal and conceived a pessimistic view of life. The day before yesterday, at 11:00 PM, he went alone to the Hankou Road pier, hired sampan No. 1001, and said he wanted to go to Pudong. When the sampan reached the middle of the river, Li jumped into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. Fortunately, the sampan operator, Chen Jinde, immediately used a bamboo pole to hook Li, allowing him to be rescued. He was then sent to the Customs Water Police Station. After the head constable inquired about the reasons for the suicide, Li stated that he worked at Guang Sheng Hong on Nanjing Road. He had met a woman named Hu Caiyun, 17 years old, from Hebei. Through friends, they developed a love relationship, and their passion reached a boiling point. "Because our private affairs cannot be a long-term plan, I discussed with her to ask a matchmaker to propose to her parents. Unexpectedly, many obstacles arose. The other party's parents are old-fashioned and sternly rejected our affair. I was unable to control my anger, and the family moved back to their ancestral home in Hebei. From then on, we are separated by vast distances, and I can only lament my helplessness. Recalling the past, I am in so much pain that I don't want to live," he said. The senior Chinese officer at the police station believed that Li's sacrifice of his young life for a woman and an unsuccessful marriage proposal was a foolish act, so he gave him detailed guidance to prevent him from repeating his mistake. The head constable then sent Detective Wu Rongsheng to escort Li to the upstairs of Chen Quan's Fate Calculation Hall on North Henan Road to be taken in by his brother-in-law, Chen Mingzhou, and severely admonished.

Four-Route Fortress Sends Personnel to Survey the Wusong Fortress Seawall 187

The Wusong Fortress's various forts are all built along the seawall. After being damaged by the recent huge tide, the situation is precarious. Fortress Commander Deng Zhenquan, believing that the matter could not be ignored, urgently telegraphed the Ministry of Military Affairs and the four-route fortress command headquarters of Ning, Zhen, Cheng, and Song, requesting that personnel be sent to conduct an on-site survey as soon as possible. After receiving the telegram, the four-route fortress specially dispatched Chief of Staff Shuai Chongxing and staff member Li Lide to the Song forts yesterday morning to inspect the actual situation. They were received by Commander Deng, and Chief of Staff Teng Wenshou and Adjutant Shen Zitian accompanied them on a week-long inspection of the north and south forts and the Lion Grove Fort. After the inspection, Chief of Staff Shuai reported back to the headquarters. It is said that funds will be allocated for repairs to strengthen the dike and defend the country.

Statistics on Traffic Accidents in the Public Concession in August 188

1,179 Cases

According to statistics from the Police Traffic Department, a total of 1,179 traffic accidents occurred in the Public Concession in August, resulting in 12 deaths and 258 injuries. Compared to only 865 cases in the same month last year, this month's number has increased by more than 300, which is alarming. It was found that 177 of the accidents last month were related to trams, 897 were related to cars, and 80 were related to buses. Among the deaths, 8 people were crushed to death by cars. The other types of vehicles caused fewer accidents. So far this year, the total number of traffic accidents in eight months has reached 8,188.

To Be Held at Ye Garden Starting September 11th

Shanghai gentlemen Wang Yiting, Wang Xiaolai, Xu Shiying, Zhu Ziqiao, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhang Weirou, Wang Binyan, Wu Zhihao, Wen Lanting, Lu Liankui, Shao Ruxin, and others have initiated a large-scale variety show. The Nan Fengxiang Robbery Case is Solved 190

On March 17th of this year, the Nan Fengxiang Jewelry Store inside the Dadongmen Gate in the jurisdiction of the Second Precinct of the First District of the Nanshi was robbed by bandits of a large quantity of gold jewelry worth several thousand gold pieces, and a box cannon carried by the petitioning police officer at the store was also seized on the spot. After the case occurred, the director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau repeatedly ordered his subordinates to intensify their efforts to track down the criminals and solve the case as soon as possible. After careful investigation by Captain Lu of the Detective Team, buying information and following leads, it was suddenly reported by team leader Shan Bin that, according to confidential sources, the bandits in this case, Gu Weiliang and others, were hiding in the thatched houses behind the Gongyi Cotton Mill in Caojiadu. Every time after work, the bandits would be near the factory teasing and having fun. He requested instructions on how to proceed. Upon hearing the news, Captain Lu immediately dispatched detectives Ding Shunbao, Wu Zuorong, Zhang Xinlong, Wu Kezhong, Shen Wenda, and Chen Liangfu to disguise themselves and lie in wait, seizing the opportunity to arrest them. It was reported by the officers that on the previous day (the 1st), after receiving instructions, they disguised themselves and went to the vicinity of the Gongyi Factory to lie in wait. At around 6:00 PM, just as the factory was letting out workers, the bandits Gu Weiliang and others were seen strolling idly. They immediately took action without showing any signs and, together with the local police, surrounded and arrested the bandits Gu Weiliang, Jin Xiaosan, and suspect Zhang Haisan on the spot. They were taken to the team, where the captain interrogated them separately. The bandits Gu Weiliang and others all confessed to robbing the Nan Fengxiang Jewelry Store with weapons. They also confessed that an accomplice, Dong Huaibao, was hiding in a house at 22 Bailinan Road. They were ordered to take the criminals back to the house and arrest Dong. After a thorough interrogation, after the truth is known, they will be sent to the Judicial Section for review.

Fire at Xia Yingtang's Home Kills an Old Servant 191

Lin Xiangxiang, a 60-year-old sedan chair carrier at the home of Xia Yingtang, a doctor of the time in Dongma Bridge on Fangbang Road in the city, was no longer able to work. Xia, remembering that he was an old servant for decades, provided him with food and accommodation at home. Yesterday at 4:00 AM, Lin was sound asleep when the mosquito incense stick he had lit burned the mosquito net. The fire immediately spread, burning the bedding. The room was filled with thick smoke, and Lin was choked unconscious by the smoke. The fire burned his skin and flesh, and he did not know which way to escape. He curled up in bed and died tragically. However, the family members had already heard the alarm and got up to put out the fire, so the house was not damaged in the slightest. Only Lin Xiangxiang was burned to death. After the incident, the Second Precinct of the First District investigated the facts and ordered a certain Hua Dechang in the Eighth Ward to report to the local court. Prosecutor Yang and others were commissioned to go to the scene to verify the facts and ordered the body to be collected for burial.

Different Accents Between Siblings 192

Abduction Case on the Fengtian Steamer

Investigators Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang of the Relief Association, together with Detective Bao Huang Songsheng of the Water Police Station, investigated an abduction case on the Taikoo Company's Fengtian steamer yesterday. They saw a young girl who was acting restless. The officers immediately questioned her. She claimed to be Wu Lanying, 16 years old, from Wuxi, living at 33 Sanxing Lane, Baxianqiao. This time, she was going to her aunt's house in Yantai with her brother. When asked about her aunt's name, she was at a loss. While they were questioning her, the so-called brother came to interfere. Unexpectedly, his accent was from Shandong. The officers were even more suspicious and questioned him. If they were siblings, why were their accents different? He claimed that the girl was born to his father's concubine. When asked where they came from, he said Nanjing, contradicting himself. The officers suddenly asked the man's name, and he said Yang Pinshan. When asked why their names were different if they were siblings, and what their parents' names were, the man said he didn't know. The officers thought it unheard of for children not to know their father's name, and arrested them together and took them to the Water Police Station for questioning. It turned out that they had abducted her from Zhujiaqiao, concocted a story, and taken her to another port. After recording the confession, the head constable transferred the group to the local court, where the prosecutor investigated and ordered Yang Pinshan to be detained and the girl to be sent to the association for safekeeping.

Police Department Does Not Recognize Private Detectives 193

Considers Them Illegal Organizations

Phone Company Theft

Private Detective Investigates

Resulting in Conviction

The China-Foreign Telephone Company on Fujian Road recently suffered repeated thefts of large quantities of telephone wires, which could not be investigated. The company commissioned Clarke's Detective Agency at 36 Renji Road to investigate on their behalf. Clarke is a British man who previously served as Deputy Inspector-General in the Public Concession's Public Works Department. After resigning due to an incident a few years ago, he founded a private detective agency. Now that Clarke has accepted the commission from the telephone company, he ordered his employee, Jin Meisheng from Suzhou, to handle the matter. Jin secretly investigated everywhere. He met the telephone company workers Ji Zhengda, Peng Caoxue, and Zheng Caohai at the Yong'an Company's rooftop garden. Jin lured them with words, claiming that he wanted to buy telephone wires. The workers, not knowing that Jin was a private detective, agreed. The next day, they secretly obtained 70 yuan worth of telephone wires from the company and sold them to Jin for profit. Jin immediately reported the information to the telephone company, which in turn reported it to the Laozha Police Station. The station dispatched detectives to arrest the three workers and sent them to the First Special District Court. After interrogation, Ji and others were sentenced to six months' imprisonment for embezzlement, with a three-year suspended sentence due to their first offense. However, after this case occurred, the police department considered Jin Meisheng's actions to be inappropriate and suspected him of violating Article 165 of the Criminal Law for obstructing order and Article 376 for receiving stolen goods. Therefore, they filed a lawsuit against Jin and sent him to the First Criminal Court of the Special Court yesterday morning, where Chief Judge Zhou Hanting presided over the hearing. Clarke also attended the hearing. The police lawyer, Ru Bao, stated the above situation, saying that according to the defendant's confession to the police, he was working as an assistant at Clarke's private detective agency. The term "private detective" is, in name, no different from a police detective. According to the regulations of the Yangjingbang, private detectives have no basis. Moreover, in the Public Concession, no police agency other than the Public Works Department can exercise police powers. Therefore, the Public Works Department absolutely denies the private detective agency and believes that it has no right to exercise its duties. Now that the defendant has exercised his duties and exercised the powers of a public official, he has violated Article 165 of the Criminal Law for obstructing order and is suspected of receiving stolen goods. Therefore, he is being prosecuted. Subsequently, the telephone company's engineer, the British man Webb, filed a complaint about the theft of telephone wires. The telephone company's representative, the British man Wilson, also filed a report stating that because of repeated thefts of telephone wires, they commissioned Clarke's private detective to investigate. Chief Judge Zhou declared to the representative that if there is a theft in the concession, it must be reported to the police station. It is inappropriate for you to abandon the police station and commission a private detective. Have you investigated whether the private detective is legal? The representative replied that he had not investigated. When asked, the defendant Jin Meisheng stated that he was ordered to go out and buy telephone wires and reported it to the telephone company, and there was nothing else. Chief Judge Zhou reviewed the confession and, considering that the private detective agency was an illegal organization and could not arbitrarily exercise its powers, sentenced the defendant Jin Meisheng in court to a fine of 150 yuan for illegally exercising the powers of a public official. If he was unable to pay the fine, he would be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed would be used to offset the fine, with one day offsetting one yuan.

The work of the Shanghai YWCA, such as the People's Night School, labor groups, and dance classes, will continue during the summer vacation. French National Kills Qu Ronglong in a Car Accident 196

Qu Ronglong, a local resident, 28 years old, opened a New Star Milk Shop at 111 Daxi Road in the western suburbs of Shanghai. At 7:30 PM the night before last, Qu was riding a bicycle No. 390 home from Xujiahui when a car No. 8777, driven by a French national named Robot, who lived at 202 Xiahui Road, turned from Daxi Road and headed south into Columbia Road, hitting Qu and his bicycle. Qu was knocked to the ground, his head was broken and bleeding, and he lost consciousness. The front wheel of the bicycle was also smashed. The Daxi Road branch of the Second Precinct of the Sixth District was nearby. The police officer, upon learning of the situation, immediately sent Sergeant Wu Dazhao to take the injured Qu Ronglong to the Chinese Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. He also took the French national Robot, who caused the accident, and the car No. 8777 back to the station. After a brief interrogation by Director Liu, he prepared a document and sent it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau overnight for investigation. However, Qu's skull was shattered and he lost too much blood. He died in the hospital yesterday evening.

Three Doctors Move to New Location for Consultations 198

Famous doctors Xu Yimin and Yu Jiandong, along with dentist Xu Junmin, have moved their clinic, formerly located at 50 Beijing Road, due to busy practices and insufficient space. They have recently moved to Suite 601-606 on the sixth floor of the Liu Hongji Building at 6 Sichuan Road. The clinic is spacious and well-appointed, with separate rooms and sophisticated equipment. There is a men's diagnosis department on the right and a women's diagnosis department on the left, as well as a surgical dissection room, a washing room, an electric light, a registration room, an information desk, and a visitor lounge. There are also male and female nurses on duty to take care of patients at all times. It is expected that the practice will flourish in the future.

▲ Dr. Xu Yimin's Brief Biography He graduated from St. John's University in 1916 with a Bachelor of Arts degree. In 1919, he received a Doctor of Medicine degree. He served at Tongren Hospital in Shanghai for one year. The following year, he went to the United States and entered the University of Pennsylvania, specializing in urology and venereology. In 1923, he received a Doctor of Medicine degree and returned to China. He was hired by Tongren Hospital as the Director of Urology and a professor of urology at St. John's Medical School.

▲ Dr. Yu Jiandong's Brief Biography He graduated from St. John's University in 1916 with a Bachelor of Science degree. In 1919, he received a Doctor of Medicine degree. After graduation, he was hired by Tongren Hospital as an assistant in internal and external medicine and a professor of anatomy at St. John's University Medical School. From 1923, he served as the director of the electrotherapy department of Tongren Hospital, the deputy director of urology, and an assistant teacher of urology at St. John's University Medical School.

▲ Dr. Xu Junmin's Brief Biography He graduated from Tokyo Dental College in 1922 with a bachelor's degree. He also served at the affiliated dental hospital for one year. The following year, he returned to Shanghai and started his own practice. He has served as an officer of the Shanghai Dental Medical Association, a dental registration review committee member of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, and the director of technicians at the Shanghai Dental Medical College.

Chronicle of the Cheng-Jiang Wedding 199

Mr. Cheng Yuqing and Miss Jiang Yaying were engaged in Shanghai years ago through the introduction of Mr. Zhu Lide and Mr. Pan Mingfeng. Yesterday, they held a wedding ceremony at the New World Hotel. Hundreds of people from all walks of life attended to congratulate them, including Chen Aishi, Pan Gongbi, Wang Yingbin, Xi Derun, Lin Huanzhang, Sheng Xiegui, Ge Gongzhen, and others. The ceremony was held at 6:00 PM. It is said that the groom is from a prominent family in Kunshan and is well-known in the news industry. The bride is the daughter of Mr. Jiang Tingfu, the owner of the Jinchang Machinery Factory. She is gentle and knowledgeable and can be called a good match. The newlyweds are scheduled to return to Kunshan today to host a banquet for local relatives and friends. Shanghai acquaintances are also among those invited, and it is expected that there will be another grand occasion.

Sales of Baokiu Brand Dry Batteries Soar 200

American Baokiu brand flashlights, using dry batteries and ordinary size six dry batteries, have long enjoyed a prestigious reputation in Europe and America. Recently, Kang Sheng Import and Export Company at No. 2 Guangdong Road in this port has become the exclusive distributor. Sales have been extremely wide in the past month. The enduring and durable characteristics of Baokiu brand are truly unique, unmatched by other brands on the market. Therefore, once customers purchase and use them, they invariably specify this brand. Electrical shops such as Tong Mao Hua, Huitong, and Lai in this port all offer wholesale, and all major companies, electrical material shops, and stores sell them.

Reader Correspondence

Mr. Wang Youren's Letter

I felt great pain in my early childhood learning. I intend to study Chinese in my spare time, but because I am bound by store regulations, I can only study by correspondence. There are very few correspondence schools in Shanghai that I know of, so I have written this letter specifically requesting your newspaper to recommend one or two places with real scholars for me to choose from.

(Reply) The Chinese Correspondence Department of the Commercial Press is divided into three levels: elementary, middle, and high school. You can directly request the regulations from the Press. In addition, the Chinese Vocational Education Society on Huanlong Road has a correspondence school with full-time teachers who use communication methods to guide learning, and you can also go there for face-to-face guidance at any time. If you are interested, you can also request a copy of the regulations for your perusal.

Mr. Yang Yin's Letter

I remember that around August 20th, your newspaper published several current commentaries on basic educational issues, discussing the difficulty students have in accessing educational opportunities, which is quite pitiful. I am one of those rejected by those dignified headmasters because I don't have tuition fees. However, even if I did, to be honest, I would not want to study in the current mechanical, commercialized schools that only care about teaching and not about the needs of the students. Therefore, I have decided on my future direction, which is to study on my own for two years and then seek employment. But what books should I study on my own during these two years? Please answer me one by one in the newspaper (I studied in high school for one year), because I imagine there must be many people who sympathize with me, and it will certainly not be a waste of your considerable energy, time, and the precious space of the Shen Bao, just for one person. Can you accept my request?

(Reply) Young people who have studied to the high school level must determine their future career direction, so that what they learn is more relevant and useful. Since you have studied in high school for one year and want to study on your own for two years, it is best to understand your own nature, talent, interests, and environment, and decide what kind of occupation you will pursue in the future. Then, when you study on your own, prepare to learn the knowledge and skills related to preparing for that occupation. Since the letter states (no tuition fees), it is not necessary to study on your own for two years. Why not seek employment early? If you are interested in supplementary schools, you should quickly prepare for a career or find a way to enter a vocational supplementary school. If you get a job, accumulate some surplus funds after a few years, and then pursue higher education, wouldn't that be taking care of both sides? Because I do not know the direction of your employment and study at this time, it is difficult to suggest a list of self-study books. Please understand.

Shen Bao Reader Correspondence Guidelines 201

The staff of this newspaper firmly believes that the readers have several personal problems that urgently need discussion. Based on the spirit of serving the society, the staff is willing to act as consultants and try to provide textual discussion with the utmost sincerity. If readers can obtain appropriate solutions, reduce some difficulties, and increase some happiness as a result, how could we not be happy?

1. The issues you wish to discuss with the staff of this newspaper are temporarily limited to the three categories of study, career, and marriage.

2. When corresponding, please first state your name, gender, age, occupation (or place of study, grade), native place, mailing address (it is still advisable to provide detailed information when continuing correspondence, for fear that previous letters may not reach you). Then, begin a new paragraph to indicate the problems you wish to discuss. The writing should be detailed, accurate, and easy to understand the true meaning. On the outside of the envelope, please write "Shen Bao Reader Correspondence Department" and attach a sufficient number of return postage stamps.

3. When corresponding, you must cut out the special printed stamp in the Reader Correspondence column of this newspaper and paste it on the upper left corner of the stationery as a ticket.

4. The processing method after this newspaper receives the letter: A. Respect the wishes of the reader. All letters stating that they hope not to be answered in the newspaper or do not wish to disclose their name when answering will be complied with. B. If the letter does not state how to answer, but the staff believes that answering one person has value for everyone to refer to, it will be disclosed in the newspaper.

C. If the letter states that it hopes to be answered in the newspaper, but it is limited by space, only the main points can be disclosed, or it may not be disclosed at all, or it may have to be disclosed later because the issue is still under consideration. Please forgive us, but if it cannot be answered in the newspaper, it will still be answered by correspondence.

(Erratum) In the report on the 9th of this month, this newspaper reported that the First Special District Court sentenced Qiao Zimen to three years in prison and a fine of one thousand yuan. A "five" character was omitted above the thousand yuan. We hereby correct this.

Weather Report 203

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The Yangtze River Basin and Shandong area are cloudy, with occasional rainfall in some areas. There is a cyclone in the Yellow Sea caused by a low pressure passing and moving towards the northeast-east. The weather on the Guangdong coast is bad because a hurricane is heading towards the northwest-west and is close to Hong Kong. There are strong southeasterly winds in the East China Sea. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 91.2 degrees, and the lowest was 76.1 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 84.6 degrees, and the lowest was 72.1 degrees.

Free Talk

Not Removing the Garden Grass, Zhai Fu's Talk Collection

Twice the Size of Newton 204

People are always happy when children are born white and fat. If they are born a little thin or dark, parents or friends will show them less affection. Most people probably have this kind of mentality to some extent. People who know a little about eugenics even arbitrarily judge the quality of seeds based on the size and strength of the body. This is wrong. People are not pigs, so how can you determine superiority based on fat and thin? The average Chinese child weighs about eight or nine pounds at birth. Recently, two of our friends had a child who weighed only six pounds. I was afraid that they would be affected by general opinions, or that they would discriminate against their little baby, so I wrote a letter congratulating them, saying:

(......I heard that you had a six-pound baby and I am very happy. For nearly 250 years, the authority who led natural science, Sir Isaac Newton, weighed only three pounds at birth. Your little baby is twice the size of Newton, and his contribution to mankind will also be twice as much. ......)

When Newton was born, everyone thought he would not survive. The two midwives who were sent to call the doctor. As they walked, they complained: (It's really stupid for us to rush like this! It would be a miracle if he could live until we get home. Such a little mouse, he will always not survive, we will run our legs swollen, and we won't get a thank you. Sister, we have no way to do this job. Heaven chose us to do this, so we have to hurry. Thank goodness, it's easy to eat to get there.) Contrary to the midwife's expectations, Newton lived, and lived to eighty-five years old. (Born in 1642, died in 1727)

Jiang Dengxuan 205

— Zhezun

Jiang Dengxuan's courtesy name was Chaoliu. He was the son of Jiang Guiti, the commander of the Yi Army. Guiti only knew a few characters. One day, he passed through the market and saw the words "Mobil Oil" plastered everywhere on the walls. Guiti said to those around him, "There are quite a few people with the surname Jiang here." He had mistakenly recognized the word "Mei" (美) as the character "Jiang" (姜). Those around him dared not laugh, but only agreed. Chaoliu was intelligent as a child. Because his father had not studied, he was quite fond of learning. He was also able to compose poetry. After entering the military, he had the style of a learned general. After the war in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, Qi Fu, the governor, went to Japan. Zhang Zongchang, Lu Zijia, and Yang Linge successively came to Jiangsu. Chaoliu was then appointed by the Feng faction as the Commander-in-Chief for Suppressing Bandits in the Four Provinces. Later, he became the Commander-in-Chief of Anhui Province. Before long, Guo Songling turned against Feng. Sun Xinyuan also led troops from Zhejiang to Jiangsu. Chaoliu had no choice but to take his troops back to Feng. On the way, he met with Guo, intending to dissuade him out of friendship. Unexpectedly, he was surrounded and killed by Guo's troops. The knife wounds were terrible. Guo was soon defeated by Zou Zuohua, the artillery brigade commander of his own troops, who turned against him. He and his wife fled secretly and were captured and executed by shooting. Chaoliu later descended to a spirit altar four times. He left many judgments. The last one was a regulated verse. The poem said: "It is sad to lose one's life in troubled times. Do not suspect each other of kindness and resentment. The overwhelming injustice is sung like a cry. The ghostly soul enters the earth and comes again. Wild flowers on the desolate tomb are born from the blood of the deceased. The snow phantom on the horizontal mountain is the ash of the catastrophe. The white bones of a stranger have been detained for many years. Who will pour a cup towards the Yellow Springs?" After the judgment, he was about to leave and said again, "Wearing armor, I will not bow. Farewell, mournfully." It is conceivable that he was refined and different. The meaning of the poem is sad and unbearable to read. I think that the calamity is difficult to escape, and it is the same in ancient and modern times. No matter what kind of person they are in the world, if they are born in troubled times, they are probably here to complete this calamity. Infighting continues. Revenge follows each other. Changeable and impermanent. Arguing endlessly. In the end, both sides are hurt. Alas, how sad!

World Anecdotes 206

— Haike

The late King Edward loved flowers very much. And what he loved most was the carnation (Shanghai flower sellers call it "Kang Na Sheng"). Although carnations are not very fragrant, they have several colors. The form of the flowers is also exquisite and lovely. What the king especially loved was a white carnation, called "Whitepearl".

▲ Sunbathing as Fashion European and American women's favorite fashions are often whimsical and change at any time. The most recent trend is sunbathing as fashion. In seaside social scenes, you can often hear a woman praising another woman: (I don't know where she got this soft sun-kissed color.) Therefore, the fashionable women on the beach and tennis court this summer often have bare, sun-tanned yellow legs. If they are not sun-tanned, they are specially dyed with a tan color. This color is said to be made into creams and pastes. On the one hand, it is trendy, and on the other hand, it is economical. Because a pair of long or short stockings can be saved.

Record of the Minotaur of Paris 207

— Huang Yingdai

The form of human beings is bizarre and strange, and there is nothing strange about it. In Paris, the capital of France, there is a Minotaur. A strange thing, too. A human body with a bull's head can speak to people. Last time at the exhibition of strange people, all the visitors were amazed when they saw it. Even the famous bearded women of Europe and America could not compete with it. Recently, this Minotaur suddenly died. He left behind a property of 14,000 pounds.

When the Minotaur was alive, he went to various places to perform. Those who wanted to see this strange person had to pay a fee of six cents to enter. However, the Minotaur's property was not accumulated from ticket sales. It was because he had invented things in mechanics and obtained patent money. He was in the United States at that time. He had already moved to the United States. He soon married and had a daughter.

After the Minotaur got married, he soon felt disgusted with his family and suffered from homesickness. One morning, he took all his belongings and left. His wife and daughter did not hear from him. After the Minotaur left the United States, he returned to his hometown in France. He soon lived with a woman and had two daughters. When he died two years ago, he left his property to his mother and daughter.

The Minotaur suddenly disappeared in the United States, and people in the society were surprised. However, his eldest daughter did not avoid hardship, traveled long distances, and crossed the Atlantic Ocean to collect all the information about her father's life. She applied to the court for a division of property. According to French law, the eldest daughter has the right to divide the property. She can get at least half of the 14,000 pounds, it is said.

Records of Interesting Things of the Time 208

— Yan Chonglou

Gu Dingmei Sang Wildly at the Banquet Gu Xiegui, courtesy name Dingmei, was a famous scholar in Jiangnan. He traveled to Shaanxi and Gansu in the past and had literary exchanges with my father. Later, he returned south to preside over the Scientific Instrument Museum. My father also lived in Shanghai, so they often visited each other. He was a forthright and unceremonious man. Here is a story he told to help the conversation along. One day, my father gathered friends for a banquet at the Wanzhao Building. Wang Yiting, Di Pingzi, Xiang Songmao, Li Zuhan, and Qiu Jun and his sister were among the guests. He was also there. After drinking for a while, he suddenly became very interested in singing. He sang the Kunqu opera "Thinking of Mortal World" wildly in the middle of the banquet. Although there was no tune or rhythm, his voice was loud and shook the roof tiles. The whole table laughed, and Mr. Yiting especially held his stomach and couldn't stop laughing.

▲ Zhang Danweng's One-Character Letter Danweng's real name was Danfu. Danweng was his pen name. He was famous in society for his good at writing strange articles and characters. He once worked for the late General Lu Langzhai, planning strategies and traveling to Chang'an together. Therefore, he was familiar with my father. When I traveled south to study, I often visited his residence during my spare time to ask for advice, and he also often invited me to talk. Therefore, there are many letters from him in my suitcase. The most peculiar thing was that he wrote a letter in a hurry, with only the word "Lai" (來, "come"). It was not addressed or signed. However, I could recognize it as his letter of invitation by the handwriting. So this simple letter was far better than a telegram.

▲ Liu Gonglu's Amazing Long Braid Liu Gonglu of Guichi had a family history of scholarship and was talented at a young age. He had a fondness for braids, so people called him the "Remnant Youth" (遺少) to distinguish him from the "Remnant Elders" (遺老). I once visited his residence and saw the calligraphy and paintings hanging on the wall with the inscription "Xuantong 78th year", so the Remnant Youth was indeed worthy of the name. Gonglu lived in the foreign concession, so he kept his long braid, and was spared the haircut of Bingzhou. However, whenever he dragged his braid through the city, people who saw him were curious and pointed and talked. He was not embarrassed at all. I remember once going with him to the municipal hall to watch a play. When the show ended, a voice suddenly rang out in the crowd: (Where did the Braid Master come from?) All the audience's attention was focused on him. He walked out of the crowd without taking offense. Now he has moved to Suzhou. I once asked a friend to visit him, and his braid was deeply hidden under his hat, not like it was in Shanghai, where it hung down behind his head and swaggered through the market.

A New Medical View of Treating Burns with Tea 209

— Yang Yebai

Burns are caused by the body coming into contact with fire, powder, steam, boiling soup, and high-temperature solids. They are most commonly encountered in daily life. The symptoms are divided into three levels. The first level is redness, swelling, and pain. The second level is blisters. The third level is tissue carbonization and loss. The drugs to treat it are nothing more than medicinal powders, ointments, pastes, and paraffin agents that have bactericidal, anti-inflammatory, and protective properties. These are all commonly used by Western medicine.

In 1924, an American named Daris discovered a toxin in the secretions of burn tissue. The bad phenomena of burns are all caused by this toxin. This toxin coagulates into a scab when it encounters tannic acid and no longer has a toxic effect. The person then used 5% tannic acid water as a dressing for burns and obtained the best treatment results. Since then, various places have followed suit and have achieved definite results. It is truly a new progress in burn therapy.

When I lived in the countryside of Guizhou in the past, it was hundreds of miles away, and there was no trace of Western medicine. After the villagers were burned, they chewed tea leaves and applied them to the injured area. If it dried, they would apply more until it scabbed over and healed. The elders passed it down and it was repeatedly tested and proven. When asked about the reason from Chinese medicine, they replied with a general term of "reducing fire and disinfecting", not knowing that tea leaves contain tannic acid. The method of applying tea is actually consistent with Dsris's theory. However, chewing tea inevitably contains toxic bacteria in the mouth, so it is better to use boiling water to brew strong tea and soak it in sterilized cotton to apply it. (Ordinary cotton can be used after steaming or boiling) It is a pity that our people do not know how to research, knowing that it is so but not knowing why. It is truly regrettable.

There are many effective Chinese prescriptions for treating diseases. Unfortunately, those who practice them often keep them secret and deceive people with strange and mysterious words. It is distorted and miscommunicated, and gradually becomes obscure. If it can be made public for precise scientific research, perhaps many medical doctors can be produced, and there can also be a considerable contribution to the world's medical community.

Qingyun Cloister and Bada Shanren (Part 1) 210

— Zheng Wuchang

In the summer of Xinwei, I visited Nanchang and heard that there was a Taoist temple called Qingyun Cloister fifteen miles southeast of the city, which was known as a scenic spot. During my leisure time, I drove there with my old friend Song Fengzi. After leaving the city, we followed the Nanchang Road. The flat fields were boundless, and the sound of threshing rice and scolding plows could be heard everywhere. It was the busy time for the first crop of farming, and the second crop was about to start. Since Ganzhou south of Fuzhou has been ravaged by the Red disaster, the cities and hills are often ruins, and no cattle or sheep can be seen in the mountains and fields for thousands of miles. Compared with this, what is the happiness and suffering of the people? Before long, we arrived at the gate. The green grass was flat and clear, and the tall wutong trees covered the eaves like a canopy. The scenery was cool. The Taoist priest Han Cuiting greeted us with great diligence. The cloister covers an area of more than ten acres and is located in the wilderness as a marshland. There are three rows of houses, a total of more than thirty rooms. The front row enshrines the statue of Guan Yu, and the system is firm and simple, like the work of the Ming Dynasty. The middle and rear rows enshrine Taoist statues. The rooms along the corridor on the left and right are Dan rooms, which are clean and spacious. It is said that they were built by the former Taoist leader Yunyan. Outside the house, there are bamboo trees and shrubs in the gaps. Water is drawn into a pond in the sunken area, and water chestnuts and lotus are planted. A plank bridge and winding paths are built to connect. The path snakes through the bamboo trees. When you are in the middle of it, a pavilion is built with wood, where you can climb up and look around. The mixed flowers and secluded birds are the opposite of what you see and hear up and down. The planning and construction of the cloister was not grand, but the arrangement was subtle, as if there was Tao in it. The customs of Jiangxi respect Taoism. The Youlong School has been spreading until now without changing. Other people do not know how to cherish it. I have not heard of Buddhist palaces. Ruziting has become a place for refugees. The Tengwang Pavilion has also been abandoned as a water management office. Those in the capital who love antiquity and seek seclusion have nowhere to set foot. Therefore, the Qingyun Taoist temple has gradually seen carriages, officials, staffs and shoes. After browsing around, we had tea under the Doumu Pavilion. The Taoist showed us the collection of Bada Shanren's calligraphy and paintings. There was only a square inch of calligraphy, running script. The painting was an axis of ancient trees and mockingbirds, ink and wash, paper. The brush and ink were not similar. It was judged to be Ying Ding. After that, the statues of the refined teacher Liangyue and Ma Quanzhen were shown. The statue of Liangyue is wearing a Taoist robe and a Confucian crown, sitting cross-legged on a Dan Cliff and green water with his eyes closed. The appearance is solemn and quiet. Taoist Wang Zehong of the Three Swords attached a eulogy to it, saying: He abandoned his family for Tian Shen to enter the sea. He boasted of Tao for his body to find fragrant beads. Taoist robe and Confucian crown, the dignity is still there. Dan Cliff and green water, what is the difference in scenery. Some think that Wang Sun is on a fork road, and some think that the universe is a rotten Confucian. Listening to the wind, I suspect that it is He Jing. Looking at the plum blossoms, it is very similar to Lin Bu. White clouds are always in the void, who can tie them down. Lingzhi is produced on the side of the cliff, and it is difficult to find a species. I don't know where Tao begins, and I don't know where Tao ends. Those who have no beginning and no end are where Tao is. Those who have no Tao in Tao are the sect of Tao. Ma Xiang had glaring eyes and a Xiu beard, bare-bellied and barefoot, sitting upright on a dangerous cliff. The shape was very tall. A crane hovered above its head. The brushstrokes of the painting are also good. There is the interest of emerging from the water and facing the wind. It is the hand of Huang Bi. San Yuan Old Man inscribed it: "A misty immortal guards the house. The altar has been prospering for thousands of years. The footsteps are like the Taoist flow. The tripod room is shining with elixir. Who is Master Ma? Where does he come from? The shore is a tall and burly figure. The silver beard is over the belly. The arms and feet are surrounded by copper rings. The divine power cannot be restrained. The chest and abdomen are proud of all kinds of monsters. Dragons, tigers, turtles and snakes are hidden. The drooping knot is so abundant. The interpretation is close to the subtle. Wonderful enlightenment reveals heaven and man. The source leads to its outline. Yang Xin's gray body. The cloud characters are shining with light. Auspicious clouds linger. The crane is not winged. The public sees and exclaims. The legends are mutually low and high. The supreme Tao still is natural. Refining the nature and frustrating the sharpness. Changes boast of the last road. Slander is everywhere. Spiritual traces shine on the earth. Occasionally hidden by the ear. Silently explore the Xuanmiao Gate. The feeling is to take the bag." Silently facing it for a long time, I lingered and could not bear to let go. The Taoist said: "The refined teacher Liangyue is the Bada Shanren. Shanren was formerly a descendant of the Ming Ning clan, named Zhu Da. After the Jia Shen change, he and his brother, whose Taoist name was Poyunzi, and his friend Ma Quanzhen, all entered Taiyi Temple as Taoist priests. They changed the name of the temple to Qingyun Cloister. Therefore, Shanren really created the Qingyun Cloister in Ganzhou at the beginning.

Fiction Fuling Society

A Husband's Wife (3) 211

— Jiang Hongjiao

She not only wanted to maintain her own personal happiness, but also sincerely wanted to preserve her husband's permanent happiness. Their marriage had not been established for long, although it was not entirely a free love, but was promoted by the half-new and old-fashioned parents' orders and matchmaker's methods, but before the marriage, neither of them was dissatisfied; especially her, she really loved her husband very deeply. When she was first married, she was very satisfied. She felt that he was a very honest young man, without any vanity or arrogance. He worked very diligently, did not love extravagance, and was very gentle to his wife. His profession was to be in constant contact with women, but apart from the time when he had to be close to women for his profession, he never hid anything from his wife, or went to hang out or talk to any woman behind his wife's back. So she trusted him very much and loved him especially. But sometimes she felt slightly that her husband was too restrained, not the attitude that a young man should have. She had many female classmates, who were very lively and beautiful. She often invited them to her house to play, to let him meet them, to talk casually, or to go on an outing, or to go to the movies together. She felt that her husband's life was too monotonous, and she wanted to use this method to make her husband's life not so boring. Sometimes she was very busy with housework, so she often asked her girlfriends to accompany her husband out to play, but Mr. Li refused at least seven or eight times out of ten. Occasionally, he agreed, but he came back alone very hastily. She was even more convinced that her husband was not worth his attention and sympathy with any woman other than his wife.

Unfortunately! The change in things was so rapid, of course, beyond her expectations. A calm lake will have a strong wind blowing up big waves. Her closest friend was Mrs. Chen, so she asked Mrs. Chen to tell Mr. Chen to investigate her husband's recent whereabouts and report to her secretly. Of course, Mrs. Chen agreed to do her best to help her, so that she would not be disappointed.

Mrs. Chen was three years younger than Mrs. Li, but her experience and skills were several times greater than Mrs. Li's, so she had already thoroughly understood Mr. Li's current attitude, and she also understood the shortcomings of Mrs. Li's usual treatment of Mr. Li, but she was unwilling to tell these things to Mrs. Li, although they were very close friends. She felt that everything between husband and wife, no outsiders can participate in the judgment or point out the right and wrong, so she did not advise Mr. Chen to do his best to help Mrs. Li; instead, she warned Mr. Chen not to interfere in other people's affairs.

Guidelines for Youth Section Submissions 213

(1) Articles should focus on discussions of youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, notes, etc. The style is not restricted.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to those concerning youth issues.

(3) Photographs should be acceptable if they relate to youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, theatrical performances and lecture tours, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements. Both individual and group submissions are welcome. Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(4) The maximum length of each article should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Manuscripts should be written horizontally. Avoid careless handwriting. Western text should be avoided if possible. If it is absolutely necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

Manuscripts will not be returned whether they are published or not. If a return is required,

(6) Do not write across the page, and do not use careless handwriting. Western text should be avoided if possible. If it is absolutely necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink for illustrations, and do not use colored paper. Use black ink on white paper.

Home
